		<title>AI Data Centers And Auto Industry Converge On Same Issues</title>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>The EV revolution relies on battery innovation, while AI data centers need a range of new energy solutions to play nice with the grid. Both sectors are taking notes.</p>
<p>The post <a href="https://semiengineering.com/ai-data-centers-and-auto-industry-converge-on-same-issues/">AI Data Centers And Auto Industry Converge On Same Issues</a> appeared first on <a href="https://semiengineering.com">Semiconductor Engineering</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">Key Takeaways</span></b><span data-contrast="auto">: </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="1" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="1" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">AI data centers need power from a range of sources, including batteries, to safeguard against blackouts, transient voltage spikes, and grid demand spikes. </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="1" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="2" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">As with regenerative braking and bidirectional charging in electric vehicles, data centers could feed power or heat back into the grid for public use, but the immediate goal is to disrupt the grid as little as possible.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="1" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="3" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">Overseeing battery and energy storage systems is a multi-tiered software management layer that monitors everything from the battery cells to the interaction between the data center and the grid.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<hr />
<p><span data-contrast="auto">AI data centers and automotive companies are converging on the same energy-related problems from different angles, but they are leveraging technology improvements developed by each other to accelerate the timetable for solutions.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Both share a common goal of obtaining more energy. For AI data centers, this is a function of insatiable demand for compute power, which is needed to shorten time to results with greater accuracy. For smart cars, which increasingly resemble data centers on wheels, it&#8217;s a matter of adding more compute-intensive intelligence and, in the case of EVs, improved range per charge.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Yet both are running into the same limitations. Power grid capacity isn&#8217;t increasing nearly as fast as demand for energy, and the technology needed to significantly improve efficiency takes time to develop. At the same time, each is encountering increased costs and political pressure stemming from rising utility rates. </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The solution comes in three parts: </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="3" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="1" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">Increasing battery storage, with bi-directional charging and sophisticated energy management, to ensure there is sufficient power available for peak loads;</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="3" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="2" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">Different materials and chip architectures that can handle higher voltages, allowing for more compute density and less data movement, and</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="3" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="3" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">More alternative energy sources to maintain power grid neutrality.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-contrast="none">Bi-directional charging is available in some vehicle models today, and it has been gaining traction as an inexpensive way of storing excess energy collected by solar panels and wind farms. Early battery storage farms utilize batteries that are considered end-of-life for vehicles because they have insufficient capacity for BEV range, but they are still useful for other applications. On top of that, battery prices have been dropping due to increased competition and new battery chemistries, which are driving new battery sales.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“As batteries become much less expensive, the growth of battery energy storage systems (BESS) will continue in a big way,” observed Peter Wawer, division president of green industrial power at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/infineon-technologies/"><span data-contrast="auto">Infineon</span></a><span data-contrast="auto">. “It&#8217;s estimated that data centers will, at a point in the future, overtake total consumption compared to the automotive market.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">An ESS, comprised of thousands of batteries managed by a battery management system, can be used as backup if the grid goes out or even voltage fluctuations, and as the main power source during peak grid times.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“AI data centers are a different beast than typical data centers,” said </span><span data-contrast="none">Sinha Puneet, senior director and global head of battery at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/mentor-a-siemens-business/"><span data-contrast="none">Siemens EDA</span></a><span data-contrast="none">. </span><span data-contrast="auto">“There are two key differentiators between a normal data center, which has been there for the last 15-plus years, versus the new AI data centers. AI data centers require a lot more joules, a lot more energy, because AI jobs are a lot more energy-consuming. Also, there is more fluctuation in energy demand for AI data centers — approximately 10X more fluctuations in energy demand compared to a regular data center — because as one AI job finishes, another comes in. If not managed correctly, fluctuation can brown out the whole grid. That&#8217;s why energy storage is extremely central for any AI data center’s operation, and that’s why you see all this massive new demand for better energy storage systems to provide that energy.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">To manage those fluctuations, fast-acting battery energy storage becomes critical, particularly if there is any disruption on the utility side. “ESS can provide energy for a few hours, but absorbing that fluctuation and providing the energy is extremely critical because these AI data centers require a lot of energy,” said Sinha. “In the U.S., you have a peak-time energy rate, which is very high. Increasingly, companies are looking at ESS to reduce their OpEx, especially the energy rate for them. They want to take away that peak-time energy consumption to batteries. A lot of normal battery energy storage systems today provide approximately one to four hours of operation. But companies are also looking at long-duration energy storage systems, such as what Google is trying to do with </span><a href="https://formenergy.com/"><span data-contrast="none">Form Energy</span></a><span data-contrast="auto">, the flow battery company.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Flow batteries are rechargeable energy management systems that store chemical energy in liquid electrolytes contained in external tanks. In the future, a longer-duration ESS will be essential to address another challenge, which is the difficulty and time-consuming process of connecting AI data centers to the grid. </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“Grid connection is an extremely time-consuming process,” said Sinha. “The last I checked, you&#8217;re looking at a few years in many cases to have that connection, which is why many companies are talking about having on-site gas generators and other power options, because it takes so long for all the compliance and whatnot to obtain the grid connection. Behind the meter, companies are looking at whether they can have on-site energy generation, as well as exploring the use of long-duration energy sources from flow batteries and other technologies that can give them longer duration operation without waiting for the grid connection.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">Managing energy movement, particularly with a mixture of equipment, is non-trivial. “How do you move a lot of energy safely, efficiently, and intelligently between the grid, storage, and highly dynamic loads?&#8221; asked Hoa Tram, senior principal product engineer at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/cadence-design-systems/">Cadence</a><span data-contrast="none">. “EVs brought us high</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">voltage battery packs, sophisticated BMS, and bidirectional power electronics for regenerative braking and vehicle</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">to</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">grid, governed by strict functional</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">safety processes — and those ideas are now showing up in data centers through large</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">scale battery energy</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">storage systems, layered battery management, and smarter interaction with the grid.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><strong>Sharing technology </strong><br />
<span data-contrast="none">What&#8217;s important to note here is the flow of ideas is not a one</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">way street. </span><span data-contrast="auto">Engineers across the electric vehicle and data center sectors are now exchanging ideas on how to optimize energy and battery use, and potentially feed excess power back to the grid in a symbiotic relationship.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">“Hyperscale data centers are leaders in using telemetry, analytics, and digital twins to plan and operate complex infrastructure, and automotive OEMs and suppliers are adopting similar approaches for software</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">defined vehicles, fleet</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">level battery analytics, and power/thermal optimization,” Tram noted. “Cadence sits in the middle of that cross</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">pollination — the same system</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">level modeling, functional</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">safety flows, and data</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">center digital twins we provide for hyperscale customers are being used to design the next generation of automotive and energy systems, as well.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">On the flip side, some vehicles already return excess power via bidirectional energy systems, including vehicle-to-grid (V2G), vehicle-to-home (V2H), and vehicle-to-load (V2L). </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“As vehicles become electric and connected, they become a moving energy asset on the road,” said Negar Soufi Amlashi, senior vice president of sales at </span><span data-contrast="auto">Infineon</span><span data-contrast="auto">. “They not only consume power, but they generate it, store it, and even feed it back to the grid. This symbiotic relationship becomes pivotal. This is a transformation, powered by semiconductors and software, enabling clean propulsion and efficient connectivity between vehicle and grid. Every single watt saved translates to value created.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Devices at play here include bidirectional traction inverters, bidirectional on-board chargers, power modules, and solid-state charging stations, based on silicon, SiC, and GaN. “This enables a power conversion which is very efficient, helps reduce losses, and makes efficiency the new currency,” Amlashi noted.  </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">AI-driven energy management makes the vehicle an essential part of the grid that can optimize power in real time. “The battery duration can be expanded by optimizing the usage of energy, which extends the range of the electric car,” said Amlashi. “Further, we enable an efficient integration of the vehicle to the grid, for example, by efficient bidirectional charging.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">With that in mind, many are asking whether data centers could achieve the same optimizations through battery energy storage systems, alternative sources of on-site power, or micro-DC grids.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“DC grids are already creeping in from the industrial side,” said </span><span data-contrast="auto">Infineon</span><span data-contrast="auto">’s Wawer. “Quite a few companies are equipping typical industrial manufacturing sites with DC grids, because the logic is very simple. You can connect consumers and gain battery storage through this kind of system, while massively increasing the efficiency. For example, today, industrial robots typically use resistors for braking. If you&#8217;re moving the arm and you have to slow it down, you brake, and you consume the energy via a resistor, which is totally inefficient. With the DC grid, you can change the topology, remove the resistor, and instead break by generation and feed the energy back into the grid — convert it like with the EV. If you break, it&#8217;s converted and fed into the battery. It opens up a huge variety of topics, including DC-fed generation, because you have some solar panels on the roof or close by. These things are already moving, slowly but steadily, in typical industrial style. That is massively being accelerated due to the AI data center guys jumping on it, so it nicely fits together.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">New materials and architectures</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{}"><br />
<span data-contrast="auto">Cranking up the voltage in systems, rather than increasing the current, is another piece of the solution. That enables greater power density per given area, and less data movement, which is expensive in terms of resources and dollars. </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Together, the semiconductor, automotive, and energy industries are exploring solutions at every layer of the stack so that cost per token remains affordable as the AI revolution continues at pace. </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“We get a lot of push on density,” said Kristof Beets, vice president of product management at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/imagination-technologies/">Imagination Technologies</a><span data-contrast="auto">. “There is a push for getting as much out of the physical space, as well as the power budgets, that data centers and automotive have. But most of the push we get is very much from the efficiency point of view. That tends to be the other markets more than the server space — the server space is still a secondary consideration.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">However, this trend may soon reverse as power needs grow, and AI inference costs rise with a focus on intelligence per watt. That will require different architectures and materials.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">According to a recent Morgan Stanley report on energy markets [1], “&#8230;investors noted that power suppliers and power equipment companies are likely to see benefits from data-center expansion, particularly among expectations that AI will unleash a productivity wave throughout the broader economy. This has investors focused on the rising demand for off-grid solutions, eliminating bottlenecks in the energy supply chain and using credit markets to finance energy system growth. While most sites also maintain their ties to the grid, investors expect to see more developers shift toward hybrid or off-grid models that let developers ensure the resilience of their operations in a tightening global power market, which places a higher focus on power equipment providers.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">That, in turn, requires new materials. “We are talking about power rails in the several thousands of amperes,” said Helmut Puchner, vice president and fellow, Aerospace &amp; Defense, at </span>Infineon Technologies<span data-contrast="auto">. “This is scaling massively. The old power supplies were single-phase power supplies. You switch your transistor on and off. Now we are talking 12 or 16 phases. Gate drivers can handle 150 amps each, or more. SiC (silicon carbide) can cover more than 1,000V. GaN (gallium nitride) is in the medium-range voltage, and silicon can cover from 650 volts down to 10 volts.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Wide bandgap materials such as SiC and GaN are enabling data centers to shift from a 48 V DC rack-level power architecture to 800V. “This is a big jump,” said Pradeep Shenoy, compute power technologist at </span>Texas Instruments<span data-contrast="auto">. “I liken it to the electric vehicle market, or vehicles in general. Today, you might have a 12V lead-acid battery. Some vehicles have 48V systems. If you look at EVs on the market today, they have batteries that are 400V or 800V. We&#8217;ve been working on that technology for quite a long time, so we&#8217;re able to quickly leverage a lot of technology around isolation or gallium nitride that was developed for other markets and apply it to data centers. Some of the architects and key leaders in the data center space will say they’re trying to borrow technology that’s already been developed for the electric vehicle market. 800V-based EVs are very common. They&#8217;re on the road today, and the infrastructure can be leveraged quickly.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">Data center vs. automotive battery management</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span><br />
Overseeing battery energy storage systems and energy management between the data center, grid, and renewable power sources is a hierarchy of AI-enabled software systems, including battery management systems (BMS), energy management systems (EMS), and grid-interactive UPS systems (GiUPS).<span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“There&#8217;s some level of energy management that&#8217;s happening at the data center, but there&#8217;s also going to be some level of coordination and communication with the power grid,” said </span><span data-contrast="auto">TI</span><span data-contrast="auto">’s Shenoy. “At a high level, it will be the data center and the grid interacting. But within a data center, there will be systems controlling how much power they pull from the grid, how much power they pull from local battery storage, or store power into it. There will be management at different levels.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">In both automotive and data center applications, the </span><span data-contrast="none">BMS monitors thermal input, hotspots, coolants, electrical controls, overcharging, or over-discharging. </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">“The thermal hydraulic cooling loop is often the most challenging,” noted </span><span data-contrast="auto">Bryan Kelly, principal engineer at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/synopsys-inc/">Synopsys</a><span data-contrast="auto">.</span><span data-contrast="none"> “This area of mechatronics typically falls outside the hands-on expertise of many hardware/software battery pack design engineers. Although CFD software tools can support preliminary ‘what if’ thermal analyses, ultimately a virtual prototype of the complete cooling system — cooling plate, piping, hoses, manifolds, and related components — is essential.” </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">Such a model enables verification across different coolant types or mixture ratios, environmental conditions, and operating scenarios, and allows results to be validated against measurement data. “In addition, an end-to-end thermal story of the battery pack simulation model makes it possible to study required heating at extremely low temperatures, evaluate HW/SW control behavior across wide temperature ranges, and simulate fault conditions — such as reduced coolant flow during high load current demand — that are difficult or impractical to reproduce on a physical test bench,” said Kelly.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">Alternative and renewable sources of power</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span><br />
The last piece of the three-part solution involves a variety of energy sources to maintain constant, uninterruptible data center power. <span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“The only solution is to have an appropriate mix of power sources, meaning solar and wind. On shorter notice, it&#8217;s most likely gas turbines that are being made available,” said </span><span data-contrast="auto">Infineon</span><span data-contrast="auto">’s Wawer. “All other forms, especially if we think about nuclear, take much too long [to build]. If I need X, Y, Z terawatt hours, and you start building a nuclear power plant, let&#8217;s see when this will be ready. The requirements are much shorter term, and the short-term availability of energy can only be supplied by renewables, plus the combination of energy storage.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Recommissioning existing nuclear plants is a faster solution. “I live in Pennsylvania, and they&#8217;re trying to reinstate the Three Mile Island nuclear power plant,” said Steven Lee, product manager of power electronics design software at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/keysight-technologies/">Keysight Technologies</a><span data-contrast="auto">. “They’re recommissioning it to power AI data centers that are coming everywhere. They&#8217;re going to continue to use the grid for distribution, but are going to rely on nuclear power to satisfy the energy demands. Electricity for you and for me, at our houses, is going to become a lot more expensive as a result of AI data centers. That will be the immediate effect for us.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">If regions do not already have nuclear, deploying solar is easier in terms of permit time, availability of solar panels, and installation. “The cost per kilowatt hour has reached a point below one cent per kilowatt,” said Wawer. “That alone should drive solar installations to be a large part of the solution going forward, to provide additional electricity as fast as possible.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The conversion power sequence to get from solar panel to battery to data center or grid is the reverse of that of grid to gate. “Solar panels create DC (using photovoltaic cells),” said Lee. “Then you&#8217;re trying to go the other way and convert it into AC using a solar inverter. That&#8217;s why it’s called an inverter, because it&#8217;s DC to AC for solar, whereas it’s an AC to DC flow to get from the electric grid to the data center processors. It’s related, but backwards.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The solar inverter can be placed before or after a battery, or both, depending on whether the system is AC-coupled or DC-coupled. The battery holds the DC charge, and then the inverter converts it to AC energy for the grid. The energy is then converted back to DC again via, for example, a two-stage 800V DC power architecture, to be used by the data center rack processors, Lee explained. </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><img data-recalc-dims="1" fetchpriority="high" decoding="async" class="alignnone size-large wp-image-24278276" src="https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/Image.jpeg?resize=1024%2C652&#038;ssl=1" alt="" width="1024" height="652" srcset="https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/Image.jpeg?resize=1024%2C652&amp;ssl=1 1024w, https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/Image.jpeg?resize=300%2C191&amp;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/Image.jpeg?resize=768%2C489&amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/Image.jpeg?resize=600%2C382&amp;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/Image.jpeg?w=1320&amp;ssl=1 1320w" sizes="(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px" /></p>
<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">Fig. 1: An EV charging from a wind and solar powered energy storage system. </span></b><a href="https://www.cadence.com/en_US/home/resources/technical-briefs/ev-efficiency-design-analysis.html"><b><span data-contrast="none">Source</span></b></a><b><span data-contrast="auto">: Cadence</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">EVs also leverage solar power, and are further along than data centers when it comes to potentially giving excess power back to the grid. For example, solar panels on the roof of a home can be connected to a Tesla wall unit. “It takes the DC solar power, charges the battery in that wall unit, then an inverter converts it to AC to charge the car or another appliance in your home,” said </span><span data-contrast="auto">Keysight</span><span data-contrast="auto">’s Lee. “Also, if the grid requires electricity from your house, because it&#8217;s short, then the power can go backwards into the grid, and then the grid can distribute that to someone else&#8217;s house, or a data center.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">It&#8217;s the same chain happening, no matter which way the power is flowing. “There&#8217;s a battery in the middle, and then instead of power coming from the grid, you could be putting it back into the grid,” said Lee. </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><img data-recalc-dims="1" decoding="async" class="alignnone wp-image-24278277 size-large" src="https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/IMG_0362.jpg?resize=1024%2C505&#038;ssl=1" alt="" width="1024" height="505" srcset="https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/IMG_0362.jpg?resize=1024%2C505&amp;ssl=1 1024w, https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/IMG_0362.jpg?resize=300%2C148&amp;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/IMG_0362.jpg?resize=768%2C379&amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/IMG_0362.jpg?resize=600%2C296&amp;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/semiengineering.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/07/IMG_0362.jpg?w=1404&amp;ssl=1 1404w" sizes="(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px" /></p>
<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">Fig. 2: Challenges in modern power grids. Source: Infineon</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">Other options</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span><br />
Similar to existing home and EV models, a data center with on-site energy generation could theoretically give excess energy back to the grid. “It depends on what sort of timescales we&#8217;re talking about,” said <span data-contrast="auto">TI</span><span data-contrast="auto">’s Shenoy. “There are some microsecond-level spikes of power that a data center might have, in very short timescales, where the grid is usually operating on much lower, longer timescales, relatively speaking. Other concerns from the power grid perspective are, ‘What if this data center has fluctuations or disturbances and takes down the power grid?’ That would not be good, and there&#8217;s a lot of activity and engineering know-how focused on ensuring the data center operates in a way that plays nicely with the grid. Even if it isn&#8217;t necessarily sending power back to the grid, if it is behaving properly as a load to the grid, that would actually be a very good accomplishment.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">A simpler possibility is to feed excess heat from data centers back to local utilities companies, as seen recently in Scandinavia. [2] [3]</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“Data centers</span> <span data-contrast="auto">are just converting energy, electrical energy, into heat, like any power plant or heating plant,” said </span><span data-contrast="auto">Infineon</span><span data-contrast="auto">’s Puchner. “I grew up in Austria, and for generations, we were burning garbage with extra fuel, and so you get rid of the garbage, and as a side product, you generate heat, which is distributed to 60,000 to 100,000 households. I can see that model being used, instead of heating the river by two or three degrees for data center cooling. Why don&#8217;t they give the heat back to the community? We can all use heat in winter.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Heating nearby facilities is technically challenging, but possible. The real issue is cost.</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“The systems exist. The technology is there. But the investment might be too high for data center companies,” said Puchner. “If the general public or governments are willing to spend that, it&#8217;s a good idea. Those data centers run 24/7 and generate a lot of heat.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Repurposing innovations look set to grow, whether they are to take advantage of excess energy or heat, or to recycle old batteries and hardware. Two recent examples: </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="2" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="1" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">Waymo transformed retired EV batteries into clean energy storage for essential local infrastructure. [4]</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="2" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="2" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">UC San Diego and Google researchers extracted motherboards of retired smartphones, collected them into clusters, and redeployed them as a general-purpose computing platform for a data center to be used by researchers and students. [5]</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">Conclusion: Why this matters</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span><br />
More efficient chip, network, and converter architectures are all part of the solution to help reduce AI data centers’ power consumption. The other side of the solution is to make use of cleaner, renewable sources of energy so that power used by AI data centers does not negatively impact the general population in terms of availability and cost. <span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Electric vehicles promise similar relief from reliance on limited oil supplies. However, it&#8217;s worth noting that depending on where a driver’s electric grid gets its power — from nuclear to hydro to coal — EVs are not necessarily a lot cleaner than gas-powered cars. “You are just looking at one very specific part of the timeline, which is my car, but you&#8217;re not looking upstream where the power comes from,” </span><span data-contrast="auto">Keysight</span><span data-contrast="auto">’s Lee noted. </span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">References</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">[1] Energy Markets Race to Solve the </span><a href="https://www.morganstanley.com/insights/articles/powering-ai-energy-market-outlook-2026"><span data-contrast="none">AI Power Bottleneck</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> (Morgan Stanley)</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">[2] Finland’s </span><a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/features/2025-05-14/finland-s-data-centers-are-heating-cities-too?embedded-checkout=true"><span data-contrast="none">Data Centers Are Heating Cities</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> Too (Bloomberg)</span><span data-ccp-props="{}"> </span></p>

		<title>Defending Against AI-Enabled Data Fusion</title>

		<guid isPermaLink="false">https://semiengineering.com/?p=24278337</guid>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>As multimodal AI fuses data from billions of devices, attackers can weaponize detailed digital twins of people or systems.  </p>
<p>The post <a href="https://semiengineering.com/defending-against-ai-enabled-data-fusion/">Defending Against AI-Enabled Data Fusion</a> appeared first on <a href="https://semiengineering.com">Semiconductor Engineering</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[<p><strong>Key Takeaways: </strong></p>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="5" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="1" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">By fusing vast amounts of white-, gray-, and black-market data, attackers can build a digital twin of a person and their environment, making targeted attacks far easier.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="5" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="2" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">The intersection of AI and cybersecurity is the data itself. Trustworthy fusion depends on authenticated, integrity</span>‑<span data-contrast="auto">checked inputs and verifiable, attributable AI outputs. </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li aria-setsize="-1" data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="5" data-list-defn-props="{&quot;335552541&quot;:1,&quot;335559685&quot;:720,&quot;335559991&quot;:360,&quot;469769226&quot;:&quot;Symbol&quot;,&quot;469769242&quot;:[8226],&quot;469777803&quot;:&quot;left&quot;,&quot;469777804&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;469777815&quot;:&quot;hybridMultilevel&quot;}" data-aria-posinset="3" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">Defending against AI-enabled data fusion hinges on strong roots of trust, encryption, secure key storage, and strict anonymization and minimization of any personally identifiable or location data that is shared.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<hr />
<p><span data-contrast="none">As AI systems grow more powerful and pervasive, they are transforming data into increasingly precise maps of people&#8217;s lives. By fusing data from various sources, attackers can construct highly detailed digital twins of individuals and their environments, making it easier to attack specific targets. And once they infiltrate the home, through routers, PCs, phones, or wearables, they can continuously harvest location and behavioral data, eroding personal privacy and even physical safety.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">At the intersection of AI and cybersecurity, the central battleground is the data itself. Trustworthy data fusion depends on authenticated, integrity</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">checked inputs and AI outputs that are verifiable and attributable. Defending against AI</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">enabled attacks on fused data hinges on strong roots of trust, robust encryption, secure key storage, and strict anonymization and minimization of any personally identifiable or location data that is shared. </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">To keep pace with evolving threats, chips and systems must themselves be secure by design. But they also need sufficient bandwidth, compute, isolation, and cryptographic infrastructure to perform continuous integrity checks and synchronization for worst</span>‑<span data-contrast="none">case loads, and ensure that no data leaks out at any step along the way. </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“AI data fusion combines data from multiple sources to give AI models a richer, more complete view, helping them generate deeper, more reliable insights,” noted David Maidment, senior director for market strategy at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/arm/">Arm</a><span data-contrast="auto">. “But this data fusion also concentrates sensitive information and can expand the attack surfaces. The more data types, owners, and systems involved, the greater the risk that one weak point could expose or corrupt the broader intelligence pool.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">This threat has been on the horizon for some time. People often click pop-ups on their screen to share data, often just </span><span data-contrast="none">to get the icon out of the way of what they&#8217;re trying to see or do. But those seemingly insignificant assents, plus a slew of bad actors seeking ways to steal data, have enabled attackers to build detailed profiles. “There&#8217;s a lot of white market, gray market, and black-market data out there, and depending on your source and your willingness to take in data from untrusted sources, or the clandestine rogue data, you can fuse all that data into a profile or a digital twin of a person,” said </span><span data-contrast="auto">Reed Hinkel, director, strategic programs, security, processor, wireless and NVM at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/synopsys-inc/">Synopsys</a><span data-contrast="auto">.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">Once a location such as a home can be monitored, Trojans can locate a particular person. “They either deposit Trojans in the home routers, or on your computer, or gain access through phishing attacks even at home,” Hinkel said. “Even though you may be trained at work, there are still members of your household who are giving away lots of data. They just don&#8217;t realize it. Sometimes it seems innocuous. Sometimes it&#8217;s literally directed to a financial outcome that you won&#8217;t like. The big issue is once they&#8217;re in the home, they&#8217;re also in your devices. If they can get into your phone, that&#8217;s even worse, because then it&#8217;s all the devices connected to and controlled by your phone.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">The idea goes well beyond just creating a digital twin or digital model of a person. Hackers can create a digital model of all your surroundings. The personal wearable IoT is especially problematic. “When I was at TI, hackers were leveraging watch data — personal fitness data — through the phone, and they were tracking soldiers as they were marching around perimeters of buildings, or locating people before the data could be anonymized,&#8221; Hinkel said. &#8220;The problem is that once you have a GPS and GPS-attached data, and you can connect that to a person, then they are 100% guaranteed to lose any semblance of privacy or personal assurance that they can&#8217;t be tracked.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">Using those digital footprints and digital data streams, it&#8217;s relatively easy to leverage AI to build a detailed model of a person. The key to addressing this is not to control the individual data streams, but to block the AI. </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">“It&#8217;s how you lay the foundation to ensure that it&#8217;s relevant and not an attack vector, because AI itself is actually the attack vector, not the individual data streams,&#8221; said Mohit Arora, senior director, architecture at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/synaptics/">Synaptics</a><span data-contrast="none">. &#8220;If you can influence data fusion at that level, you effectively influence the output, and you will no longer need the raw data.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">AI has fundamentally changed data fusion. “Data fusion before AI was straightforward,” Arora said. “All you cared about was confidentiality, about what you were doing and how you were doing it. Data fusion with AI is creating the intelligence. That&#8217;s the biggest part. Essentially, it&#8217;s binding all these individual data streams together to create local intelligence. Now, you have to protect this intelligence in a very different way as it enters the overall AI data pipeline. This wasn&#8217;t the conventional problem in typical data fusion because you were already aware of the individual data sets, and federated AI is just a mathematical operation. But here, since this could affect how your model behaves, you no longer care whether someone will steal your data. They can, but if they can influence the output, they don&#8217;t need to steal the data. This changes the whole landscape, because now you&#8217;re dealing with all the runtime stuff, and as with the AI pipeline, you&#8217;re doing all the inference back and forth, going to the memory channel and reading it, and compute, and so on. It&#8217;s quite a bit of runtime data manipulation. And that actually has a much larger attack surface than the conventional compute side, where you just go to secure boot and call it a day.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">Data fusion in automotive</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span><br />
<span data-contrast="auto">This becomes particularly worrisome in safety-critical applications such as automotive. With zonal architectures consolidating multiple sensor and software workloads onto shared compute, AI data fusion is rapidly becoming standard. </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“It is a key component of next-generation vehicle autonomy, but it also increases the car&#8217;s attack surface,” said Rob Fisher, senior director of product management at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/imagination-technologies/">Imagination Technologies</a><span data-contrast="auto">. “To manage this, one of the key architectural trends that is emerging as workloads centralize is the isolation of safety-critical and non-safety workloads to prevent cross-domain access and deliver freedom from interference between workloads. This is a de-risking strategy, a means to make sure that any fault or vulnerability in one area is contained, and that the vehicle can continue to operate safely.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Imagination uses hardware virtualization technology for such situations. “It assigns each VM a dedicated hardware interface and OSID-tagged memory transactions, enforced via the system MMU to prevent cross-domain access,” Fisher noted. “This is backed by built-in QoS, prioritization and deadline-based pre-emption, including protection against denial-of-service workloads, to help ensure safety-critical applications maintain deterministic performance and mitigate the impact of faulty or malicious workloads.&#8221;</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The big issue with AI data fusion is that it amplifies cybersecurity risk by combining an inference model from multiple, semi-independent data sources (e.g., environmental sensors) that were not necessarily designed to work together or to trust each other. “It is difficult to know a priori how the resulting model is going to respond if one of those data sources is compromised (e.g., starts injecting malicious data into a system far different from the nominal data ingested during model training),” explained Scott Best, senior technical director, Security IP at </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/rambus-inc/">Rambus</a><span data-contrast="auto">. “In a sense, you’re attempting to protect against previously unknown, black-box interactions between many disparate systems.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The first time Sylvain Guilley, fellow and CTO at </span>Secure-IC<span data-contrast="auto">, a </span><a href="https://semiengineering.com/entities/cadence-design-systems/">Cadence</a><span data-contrast="auto"> company, encountered AI data fusion was in the automotive industry, working for a chip company in Israel that was doing image analysis for multiple cameras. “My activity at the time was on the security of those kinds of chips and understanding what they were doing. It was an automotive project, and they were asking for a hardware security module (HSM). In automotive, it&#8217;s all about safety, so you want to ensure the chips cannot be initialized or provisioned by anyone. This is the first line of defense against attackers, so you want to own your chip. That&#8217;s the HSM, which means you cannot use the chip or set the firmware and configuration unless you are the legal owner. We delivered the HSM, and then they said, ‘We have a problem because now the traffic will be one gigabit per second.’ We were a little bit surprised because the HSM was configured to perform secure boots, take finite-size images, verify the signature, and now they were telling us, ‘Now we will have to manage some streaming data.’ Then they said they needed another mailbox because they were multiplying the number of cameras. It was incoming IPsec (Internet Protocol Security) traffic, and we were asked, because it was an ASIL B project, how to secure streaming data at speed. One of the initial concerns was losing a packet or a frame. Because I was managing the chip level, I couldn&#8217;t see the full application, but I could imagine that if you are a little bit desynchronized, and your car is lagging with where it is compared to what it thinks it is, that is scary. So, we worked to avoid any latency and any desynchronization, such as dropping packets, etc.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><b><span data-contrast="auto">What AI data fusion means to a chip architect</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span><br />
<span data-contrast="auto">AI data fusion requires enforcing trust in real time and at scale, and that needs to be architected into the design. “The risk is not just data exposure, but operational integrity,” said Rambus’ Best. “If an attacker can compromise one input stream, even with subtle bias, they potentially can influence the entire model output. You need a chain of trust that starts in silicon and extends outward. Root of trust in hardware, system-level attestation, and authenticated components in the supply chain must all align. If any stage cannot prove its integrity, the whole system is suspect. The chip must enforce trust and never assume it.” </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">That starts with a hardware root of trust, isolated execution, and authenticated data movement between blocks. “If every data source is cryptographically verified (including hardware and software attestation), and authenticated before being allowed to source an input into an inference operation, you shrink the attack surface an attacker can exploit,&#8221; Best said. &#8220;Beyond the strong hardware root of trust, protected key storage, and protections for secure supply-chain concepts, an indelible, tamper-resistant cryptographic hardware is also needed that can extend its trusted operations to transform untrusted software into something worthy of consideration by a high-level inference engine. Without a structured, specific path to trusted hardware, everything executing in software is built on an insecure foundation.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">Databases and keys need to be encrypted, and any technologies that require facial or biometric activation need to be checked for potential compromise. “We&#8217;re going to see multiple stages, like multi-factor authentication for humans,&#8221; said Hinkel. &#8220;You&#8217;re going to start seeing it more for devices, and you&#8217;re going to have perhaps multiple ways to establish a root of trust. At the end of the day, there are technologies available for secure storage, including PUFs (physically unclonable functions), key wrapping, and storing keys in an encrypted, scrambled state. That adds another layer of protection that wasn&#8217;t available until we started enabling it. On top of that is the cryptography, making sure that your device is post-quantum ready, because quantum days are likely here much sooner than we think. The device industry is still at various levels of coming to grips with it, but they acknowledge that. Still, there are major problems with adding it late.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Arm’s Maidment said that chip architects should consider what role hardware should play in establishing trust. That includes how to process sensitive, multi-source data without exposing it to unauthorized software, infrastructure operators, or other workloads sharing the same system. “Hardware-backed security provides an important foundation to this problem space. Roots of trust, memory protection, secure boot, attestation, and confidential computing can all help verify the platform, isolate sensitive workloads, and protect/attest data while it is being processed.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Arm’s Confidential Compute Architecture (CCA), for example, enables workloads to run within a hardware-isolated area, restricting visibility of such workloads to privileged software and other tenants. Attestation, meanwhile, allows data owners to verify that their data is being processed by the intended software and to ensure the integrity of the data sets themselves.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">No single security measure is sufficient by itself. AI data fusion requires a combination of approaches. “Hardware isolation helps protect data while it is being processed, but organizations must also ensure the integrity and provenance of the data being combined, apply appropriate access controls, secure software supply chains, and protect communications between systems and devices,” Maidment said.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Regardless of data type or weakness, the same general rules apply, including:</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-contrast="auto">Processes that are secure by design and monitored after deployment;</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></li>
<li><span data-contrast="auto">Compliance with quality norms and best practices, while embracing regulations;</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></li>
<li><span data-contrast="auto">General data protection, including data authentication and integrity checking, and</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></li>
<li><span data-contrast="auto">Specific data protections against data stream synchronization and correct ordering, as in splicing attacks.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">“It&#8217;s not a question of chips,&#8221; Guilley said. &#8220;You&#8217;re talking about AI, and if you compare layer 1 to 3 to layer 7, when you understand that the data and everything will need to go to the processing unit, at the end of the day we go through some transistors. We must ensure that we have enough bandwidth, compute speed, and capability to perform all those checks, including signature verification, as well as the checks necessary to ensure the timestamps are well aligned. You must also make sure you have proper silos. You might have different streams that you don&#8217;t want to combine. For some of them, you want to perform correlation, but for other streams it would be a safety issue to mix or swap them. You know you will get data at a certain rate, and the worst case is 1 gigabit per second, with small packets and key rolling for every packet. You must maintain the ability to perform decapsulation and integrity verification without stalling or dropping packets. This means it&#8217;s a system-level, data-flow-oriented system. If the data is not flowing through this node, the beauty of the internet is that it will find a way. But at the end of the day, the quality of service might not be as good as you expect, whereas in automotive, when you design a chip, you must design it for the worst case, and security is on the critical path. Cybersecurity is all about risk analysis, and if you underestimate the risks, your analysis can be biased.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="none">The challenge here is understanding the combinatorial risk. “The data classification problem is a big risk, and integrity attacks have become much more dangerous than simple data theft, because in a typical architecture you can think you can keep your data confidential,” Synaptics’ Aurora noted. “I think, ‘I&#8217;m going to encrypt it,’ but if you can influence or glitch your fused data, then it&#8217;s not good. And how are you going to check the integrity of the fused data, since that&#8217;s all dealing with models and activation? You&#8217;ve got to make sure the data that&#8217;s being fused is integrity-protected. So, integrity becomes a bigger problem to deal with, and I don&#8217;t think the industry is paying much attention to it because it&#8217;s a harder problem on the memory side. The model becomes the target, because if the attacker can manipulate the fused input, they can influence the inference, in particular. Then the model is useless and more dangerous.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><b><span data-contrast="none">Conclusion</span></b><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span><br />
<span data-contrast="auto">Looking ahead, as agentic AI workloads increasingly combine data from multiple sources, building confidence in both the processing environment and the data itself will become essential, Arm’s Maidment noted. “Security features built into the chip provide the critical foundation for that trust, helping organizations process sensitive data while reducing exposure to infrastructure-level threats.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">But AI data fusion also raises broader questions about where AI and cybersecurity intersect. “How do we make AI and cybersecurity intersect, rather than superimposing them so they don&#8217;t touch? Where and what are the touch points? Even taking one step back, what is AI? AI is about dealing with data,&#8221; Guilley said. &#8220;You take data and turn it into a model, generate something, and infer. You might also have some generated data that reinforces, but it&#8217;s about what you work on, which is data, obviously, and multimodal. Then, what is cybersecurity? Cybersecurity is the science of protecting data. Cybersecurity is not protecting your car. It is not protecting you as a driver or anyone in the car. Cybersecurity is about protecting data. So, the intersection of cybersecurity and AI is data. And what we need to have in place is very simple — check data in and authenticate data out.”</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><b>Related Articles</b><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span><br />
<a href="https://semiengineering.com/agentic-ai-is-changing-data-center-architectures/"><span data-contrast="none">Agentic AI Is Changing Data Center Architectures</span></a><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span><br />
<span data-contrast="auto">Standalone GPUs are being replaced by heterogeneous SoCs and chiplets that combine CPUs, GPUs, and NPUs to eliminate memory bottlenecks, reduce latency, and boost efficiency.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span></p>
<p><a href="https://semiengineering.com/executive-outlook-agentic-ais-impact-on-chip-design/"><span data-contrast="none">Executive Outlook: Agentic AI’s Impact On Chip Design</span></a><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}"> </span><br />
